25:T822,<entryFree id="n43967" key="النَّسَا" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">النَّسَا</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> [vulg. <foreign lang="ar">عِرْقُ النَّسَا</foreign>, app. <hi rend="ital">The sciatic vein;</hi>] <hi rend="ital">the portion, in the thigh, of the vein</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">عِرْق</foreign>) <hi rend="ital">which, in the back, is called the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">وَتِين</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">and which extends to the shank, where it is called the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">صَافِن</foreign>: (IAth, TA, voce <foreign lang="ar">أَبْهَرُ</foreign>:) or the <foreign lang="ar">صاَفِن</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">عرق النسا</foreign> are <hi rend="ital">two branches of one</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عِرْق</foreign> [or <hi rend="ital">vein</hi>]: (Ibn-Seenà, vol. i. book iii. p. 608: [where the opening of each of these to let blood is mentioned:]) [in a solid-hoofed animal,] <foreign lang="ar">النسا</foreign> is <hi rend="ital">a vein</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">عِرْق</foreign>) <hi rend="ital">proceeding from the hip,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">haunch, lying within each thigh, then passing by the hock, so as to reach the hoof: when the breast is fat, each of its thighs becomes cleft by two large portions of flesh, and the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">نسا</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">runs between them, and is apparent.</hi> (S.) [In the present day it seems to be applied by some to the <hi rend="ital">sciatic nerve:</hi> and <foreign lang="ar">عِرْقُ النَّسَا</foreign>, as also <foreign lang="ar">النَسَا</foreign> alone, often signifies <hi rend="ital">sciatica,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">hip-gout:</hi> see <foreign lang="ar">نِقْرِسٌ</foreign> and also <foreign lang="ar">شَنِجٌ</foreign>.
